				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant_Technology_Solutions&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Cognizant Technology Solutions">Cognizant Technology Solutions</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the general term, see <a href="/wiki/Cognizance_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Cognizance (disambiguation)">Cognizance</a>.  For the co-founder of Australian company Cognescent Corporation, see <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Reardon" title="Thomas Reardon">Thomas Reardon</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"CTSH" redirects here. For the human gene CTSH, see <a href="/wiki/Cathepsin_H" title="Cathepsin H">Cathepsin H</a>.</div>

<p><b>Cognizant</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> that provides IT services, including digital, technology, consulting, and operations services. It is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Teaneck,_New_Jersey" title="Teaneck, New Jersey">Teaneck</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Cognizant is part of the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ-100" title="NASDAQ-100">NASDAQ-100</a> and trades under CTSH.  It was founded as an in-house technology unit of <a href="/wiki/Dun_%26_Bradstreet" title="Dun &amp; Bradstreet">Dun &amp; Bradstreet</a> in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-mishra_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mishra-4">[4]</a></sup> and started serving external clients in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-mishra_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mishra-4">[4]</a></sup></p><table href="http://www.cognizant.com">www<wbr></wbr>.cognizant<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>After a series of corporate re-organisations there was an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>Cognizant had a period of fast growth during the 2000s, becoming a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> company in 2011. The company has been involved in a number of controversies in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<p>Cognizant began as Dun &amp; Bradstreet <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_Satyam" title="Mahindra Satyam">Satyam</a> Software (DBSS),<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DBSSRenamed_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DBSSRenamed-7">[7]</a></sup> established as <a href="/wiki/Dun_%26_Bradstreet" title="Dun &amp; Bradstreet">Dun &amp; Bradstreet</a>'s in-house technology unit focused on implementing large-scale IT projects for Dun &amp; Bradstreet businesses. In 1996, the company started pursuing customers beyond Dun &amp; Bradstreet.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-contrarian_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-contrarian-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>In 1996, Dun &amp; Bradstreet spun off several of its subsidiaries including Erisco, IMS International, <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilot_Software" title="Pilot Software">Pilot Software</a>, Strategic Technologies and DBSS, to form a new company called Cognizant Corporation. Three months later, in 1997, DBSS renamed itself to Cognizant Technology Solutions. In July 1997, Dun &amp; Bradstreet bought Satyam's 24% stake in DBSS for $3.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-nomodestambitions_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nomodestambitions-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Headquarters were moved to the United States, and in March 1998, <a href="/wiki/Kumar_Mahadeva" title="Kumar Mahadeva">Kumar Mahadeva</a> was named CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Operating as a division of the Cognizant Corporation, the company focused on Y2K-related projects and web development.<sup id="cite_ref-intldir59_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intldir59-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In 1998, the parent company, Cognizant Corporation, split into two companies: <a href="/wiki/IMS_Health" title="IMS Health">IMS Health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> After this restructuring, Cognizant Technology Solutions became a public subsidiary of IMS Health. In June 1998, IMS Health partially spun off the company, conducting an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> of the Cognizant stock. The company raised $34 million, less than what the IMS Health underwriters had hoped. They earmarked the money for debt payments and upgrading company offices.<sup id="cite_ref-intldir59_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intldir59-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>Kumar Mahadeva decided to reduce the company's dependence on Y2K projects: by Q1 1999, 26% of company's revenues came from <a href="/wiki/Y2K" class="mw-redirect" title="Y2K">Y2K</a> projects, compared with 49% in early 1998. Believing that the $16.6 billion <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="Enterprise resource planning">enterprise resource planning</a> software market was saturated, Kumar Mahadeva decided to refrain from large-scale ERP implementation projects. Instead, he focused on applications management, which accounted for 37% of Cognizant's revenue in Q1 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-contrarian_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-contrarian-8">[8]</a></sup> Cognizant's revenues in 2002 were $229 million, and the company had zero debt with $100 million in the bank.<sup id="cite_ref-intldir59_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intldir59-12">[12]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dotcom bust</a>, the company grew by taking on the maintenance projects that larger IT services companies did not want.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cognizant_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="Cognizant's old logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Cognizant_logo.svg/220px-Cognizant_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="67" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="240"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 67px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Cognizant_logo.svg/220px-Cognizant_logo.svg.png" data-alt="Cognizant's old logo" data-width="220" data-height="67" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Cognizant_logo.svg/330px-Cognizant_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Cognizant_logo.svg/440px-Cognizant_logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cognizant_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cognizant's old logo</div></div></div>
<p>In 2003, IMS Health sold its entire 56% stake in Cognizant, which instituted a <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_rights_plan" title="Shareholder rights plan">poison pill</a> provision to prevent <a href="/wiki/Hostile_takeover" class="mw-redirect" title="Hostile takeover">hostile takeover</a> attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-intldir59_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intldir59-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Kumar Mahadeva resigned as the CEO in 2003, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Narayanan" title="Lakshmi Narayanan">Lakshmi Narayanan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Gradually, the company's services portfolio expanded across the IT services landscape and into <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Business process outsourcing">business process outsourcing</a> (BPO) and <a href="/wiki/Management_consulting" title="Management consulting">business consulting</a>. Lakshmi Narayanan was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_D%27Souza" title="Francisco D'Souza">Francisco D'Souza</a> in 2006. Cognizant experienced a period of fast growth during the 2000s, as reflected by its appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine's "100 Fastest-Growing Companies" list for ten consecutive years from 2003 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2014, Cognizant struck its biggest deal, acquiring healthcare IT services provider TriZetto Corp for $2.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Cognizant Shares, rose nearly 3 percent in pre-market trading.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>On 24 June 2015, the company signed a multimillion-dollar agreement with <a href="/wiki/Escorts_Group" title="Escorts Group">Escorts Group</a> in India to help Escorts' businesses in digital transformation and modernizing its operations across all business segments.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p><p>On 30 June 2015, it partnered with <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>-based supermarket retailer <a href="/wiki/NTUC_FairPrice" title="NTUC FairPrice">NTUC FairPrice</a> to perform digital transformation in NTUC's business to improve personalized and consistent customer service across multiple channels.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2018, Cognizant and a consortium of Indian life insurers announced their development of a blockchain solution aimed at increasing efficiency through facilitating cross-company data sharing. The platform which is built on Corda, a DLT platform developed by R3 was claimed to reduce dependency on third-party data intermediaries and aggregators for obtaining consumer profiles and policy details such as KYC due diligence, financial and medical underwriting, risk assessment, fraud detection and regulatory compliance.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acquisitions" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">

<td><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Services" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Cognizant provides information technology, information security, consulting, ITO and BPO services. These include business &amp; technology consulting, <a href="/wiki/Systems_integration" class="mw-redirect" title="Systems integration">systems integration</a>, application development &amp; maintenance, IT infrastructure services, analytics, <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_warehousing" class="mw-redirect" title="Data warehousing">data warehousing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a>, engineering &amp; manufacturing solutions, <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="Enterprise resource planning">enterprise resource planning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> outsourcing, and <a href="/wiki/Software_testing" title="Software testing">testing</a> solutions.
</p><p>Cognizant has three key areas of expertise which makes up their business — Digital Business, Digital Operations, and Digital Systems &amp; Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_model">Business model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Business model" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cognizant-Chennai.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cognizant-Chennai.jpg/220px-Cognizant-Chennai.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Cognizant-Chennai.jpg/220px-Cognizant-Chennai.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cognizant-Chennai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cognizant's original corporate headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, now an offshore delivery center.</div></div></div>
<p>Like many other IT services firms, Cognizant follows a <a href="/wiki/Global_delivery_model" title="Global delivery model">global delivery model</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Offshore_software_R%26D" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore software R&amp;D">offshore software R&amp;D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Offshore_outsourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore outsourcing">offshore outsourcing</a>. The company has a number of <a href="/wiki/Offshore_development_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore development center">offshore development centers</a> outside the United States and near-shore centers in the U.S., Europe and South America.
</p><p>In its early years, Cognizant gained business from a number of American and European companies with the help of the Dun &amp; Bradstreet brand. The company's senior executives envisaged the firm as a provider of high-end customer services on-par with the six contemporary major <a href="/wiki/System_integrator" class="mw-redirect" title="System integrator">system integrators</a> (<a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>, <a href="/wiki/BearingPoint" title="BearingPoint">BearingPoint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capgemini" title="Capgemini">Capgemini</a>, <a href="/wiki/E%26Y" class="mw-redirect" title="E&amp;Y">E&amp;Y</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a> and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>), but at lower prices.<sup id="cite_ref-The-India-Way-2010_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The-India-Way-2010-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Regions" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company has 310,939<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> employees globally, of which over 150,000 are in India across 10 locations with a plurality in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>. The other centers of the company are in <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore" title="Coimbatore">Coimbatore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indore" title="Indore">Indore</a>,<a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noida" title="Noida">Noida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mangalore" title="Mangalore">Mangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pune" title="Pune">Pune</a>. The company has local, regional, and global delivery centers in the UK, Hungary, The Netherlands, Spain, China, Philippines, Canada, Brazil, Argentina, Mexico etc.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_units">Business units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Business units" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cognizant is organized into several <a href="/wiki/Vertical_market" title="Vertical market">verticals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_market" title="Horizontal market">horizontal</a> units. The vertical units focus on specific industries such as Banking &amp; Financial Services, Insurance, Healthcare, Manufacturing and Retail. The horizontals focus on specific technologies or process areas such as Analytics, mobile computing, BPO and Testing. Both horizontal and vertical units have <a href="/wiki/Business_consulting" class="mw-redirect" title="Business consulting">business consultants</a>, who together form the organization-wide Cognizant Consulting team. Cognizant is among the largest recruiters of MBAs in the industry; they are involved in <a href="/wiki/Business_development" title="Business development">business development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_analysis" title="Business analysis">business analysis</a> for IT services projects.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Management" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cognizant is led by Brian Humphries (CEO), Karen McLoughlin (CFO) and Malcolm Frank (President, Cognizant Digital Business).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>On 1 April 2019, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_D%27Souza" title="Francisco D'Souza">Francisco D'Souza</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Humphries_(IT_businessman)" title="Brian Humphries (IT businessman)">Brian Humphries</a> as the CEO.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Finance" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

After the close of trading on 16 November 2006, Cognizant moved from the mid cap <a href="/wiki/S%26P_400" title="S&amp;P 400">S&amp;P 400</a> to the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Cognizant became a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> company in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_social_responsibility">Corporate social responsibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate social responsibility" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Cognizant's philanthropic and <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a> (CSR) initiatives are conducted through the Cognizant employees for the financial and administrative support of the Cognizant Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Registered in March 2005 as a "Charitable Company" under the Indian Companies Act, the Cognizant Foundation aims to help "unprivileged members of society gain access to quality education and healthcare by providing financial and technical support; designing and implementing educational and healthcare improvement programs; and partnering with <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">Non-Government Organizations</a> (NGOs), educational institutions, healthcare institutions, government agencies and corporations".
</p><p>Cognizant has a grassroots corporate social responsibility project called <i>Outreach</i>, for which Cognizant's employees volunteer to support schools and orphanages.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>At the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Maker_Faire" title="Maker Faire">Maker Faire</a>, the company announced plans to fund a <i>Maker Space</i> at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Hall_of_Science" title="New York Hall of Science">New York Hall of Science</a>, a <i>Making the Future</i> after-school program and a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Schools" title="Citizen Schools">Citizen Schools</a> to promote <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM education</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>Cognizant's sustainability efforts include a <i>Go Green</i> initiative launched in 2008 focused on <a href="/wiki/Energy_conservation" title="Energy conservation">energy conservation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a>, and responsible <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In October 2012, <i>Newsweek</i> magazine ranked Cognizant 50th among the 500 largest publicly traded companies in America, in its annual Green Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Awards" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, the <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> named it as the world's fourth most admired <a href="/wiki/IT_services" class="mw-redirect" title="IT services">IT services</a> company.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2017, Cognizant was named in <i>Fortune</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Future 50 list.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: India" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bribery">Bribery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bribery" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Larsen &amp; Toubro Ltd (L&amp;T) paid million in bribes to Indian government officials on behalf of Cognizant Technology Solutions Corp. to secure permits, ranging from environmental clearance to power. L&amp;T has made illicit payments and Cognizant reimbursed the money by disguising it as compensation for cost overruns.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Companies_Act_violations">Companies Act violations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Companies Act violations" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In March 2019, significant publicity was raised because Cognizant repetitively violated the directives of the Registrar of Companies. The Company "has moved [sic] the Madras High Court fearing possibility of criminal prosecution being launched against it by [the] Registrar of Companies for alleged violation of the provisions of the Companies Act of 2013 and the Companies (Appointment and Disqualification of Directors) Rules of 2014."  One of those questions was as to why the company had not disclosed complete information on stock options of its parent holding company — CTS Corporation in the United States — having been given to the employees, including its directors, and the payments running to several hundred crores of rupees (approx US $40 million) having been paid to the parent company in the US towards stock compensating recharge.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrimination">Discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Discrimination" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2018 a race discrimination suit was brought: "Three hundred former employees claim they were forced out of their jobs and replaced with 'less qualified' Indians after being poorly treated by their Indian supervisors and colleagues, given unjustifiably low performance ratings and denied promotions." Cognizant said it was "national origin" and not race.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Layoffs">Layoffs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Layoffs" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>20 senior executives, above the Director's Level were dismissed because they were not able to catch up with the latest technologies. The number of the executives that were dismissed is unusually high and questions the ability of the company to catch up with the latest technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>In 2017, eight employees filed petitions with the labor department, complaining Cognizant forced them to resign as part of a performance-based review. The labor department closed the case in favor of employees and advised company management to give one more opportunity for the petitioners to prove themselves. At the time Cognizant had also rolled out a ‘voluntary separation program’ for directors, associate vice-presidents and senior VP's which offed them 6–9 months of their salary.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>In 2017, approximately 60000 Cognizant employees in Hyderabad/Bangalore/Chennai lost their job as a part of company's annual performance review process.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_evasion">Tax evasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tax evasion" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The Income Tax department has frozen Cognizant Technology Solutions Corp's bank accounts and deposits in Chennai and Mumbai for allegedly evading a dividend distribution tax (DDT). A Cognizant spokesman confirmed the report and said in a statement that a court has instructed the tax department not to take further action pending further hearings. Cognizant failed to pay the tax of more than 25 billion rupees ($385 million) in the 2016-17 financial year, the Hindu newspaper reported, citing officials from the tax department.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>The court asked the company to deposit 15 percent of the disputed tax, amounting to 4.9 billion rupees ($75 million) as security deposit till it decides on the case.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ireland" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_conditions">Working conditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Working conditions" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In February 2018 the UK and Irish press expressed concerns about contractors employed by Cognizant in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> as part of the outsourcing contract with Google about the conditions of employment in relationship to compensation and basic employment allowances like sick leave.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United States" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Corruption" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2016, Cognizant announced that it was cooperating with US authorities in an investigation related to the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Corrupt_Practices_Act" title="Foreign Corrupt Practices Act">Foreign Corrupt Practices Act</a>, and carrying out its own probe to determine whether some payments made in India breached the law. The company also said President Gordon Coburn had resigned and would be replaced by Rajeev Mehta.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Crawford_.26_Company_lawsuit"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crawford_&amp;_Company_lawsuit">Crawford &amp; Company lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Crawford &amp; Company lawsuit" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Cognizant has been sued by Crawford &amp; Company, the US-based independent providers of insurance claims-handling services, for alleged breach of contract. Cognizant had been mandated by Crawford to implement People Soft Financials software as part of an ERP project called Project Atlas that it was critical to Crawford's operations. Project Atlas included components for both internal operations and client-facing services.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="H-1B_visa_violations">H-1B visa violations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: H-1B visa violations" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Cognizant leads the ranks of <a href="/wiki/H1B_visa#Employers_ranked_by_H-1B_visas_approved" class="mw-redirect" title="H1B visa">companies receiving H-1B visas</a> from the United States. The company has been steadily increasing its U.S. work force. In January 2011, the company announced plans to expand its U.S. delivery centers, including a new 1,000-person (0.4% of worldwide workforce) facility in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In February 2011, Cognizant said it had 60 full-time recruiters actively hiring in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Labor" title="United States Department of Labor">US Department of Labor</a> (DoL) found Cognizant in violation of the H-1B provisions of the Immigration and Nationality Administrative Act. 67 of its workers underpaid due to unintentional administrative errors, according to Cognizant. The DoL investigation revealed that Cognizant had achieved 99.7% compliance in its management of H-1B visa-related issues.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The company paid US$509,607 in back wages to the 67 employees.  No fines or visa restrictions were imposed, since DoL did not discover any willful violations. Joseph Petrecca, the director of the Wage and Hour Division's Northern New Jersey District Office, praised the company for taking immediate steps to correct the violations: "This level of cooperation sets a standard for others in the industry."<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p><p>In 2016, the company was the subject of a lawsuit by workers for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a> who said workers from India were brought into the United States on H-1B visas in order to replace them.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> However, in October 2016, federal Judge Gregory A. Presnel of the United States District Court in Orlando dismissed the lawsuits, stating "none of the allegedly false statements put at issue in the complaint are adequate."<sup id="cite_ref-The_New_York_Times_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_conditions_and_mental_health_issues">Working conditions and mental health issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Working conditions and mental health issues" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Facebook#Moderators" title="Criticism of Facebook">Criticism of Facebook § Moderators</a></div>
<p>In February 2019, an investigative report by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a></i> described poor working conditions in Cognizant's <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, office.<sup id="cite_ref-Trauma_Floor_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trauma_Floor-128">[128]</a></sup> Cognizant employees tasked with <a href="/wiki/Content_moderation" class="mw-redirect" title="Content moderation">content moderation</a> for <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> developed <a href="/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a> issues, including <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a>, as a result of exposure to <a href="/wiki/Graphic_violence" title="Graphic violence">graphic violence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">hate speech</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a> in the videos they were instructed to evaluate.<sup id="cite_ref-Trauma_Floor_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trauma_Floor-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Moderators at the Phoenix office reported <a href="/wiki/Drug_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Drug abuse">drug abuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_abuse" title="Alcohol abuse">alcohol abuse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a> in the workplace, and feared retaliation from <a href="/wiki/Termination_of_employment" title="Termination of employment">terminated</a> workers who threatened to harm them.<sup id="cite_ref-Trauma_Floor_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trauma_Floor-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In response, a Cognizant representative stated the company would examine the issues in the report.<sup id="cite_ref-Trauma_Floor_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trauma_Floor-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p><i>The Verge</i> published a follow-up investigation of Cognizant's <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>, office in June 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Employees in the Tampa location described working conditions that were worse than the conditions in the Phoenix office.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Content moderator Keith Utley suffered a <a href="/wiki/Heart_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart attack">heart attack</a> while working for Cognizant in March 2018 and died in a hospital; the Tampa office lacked an on-site <a href="/wiki/Defibrillator" class="mw-redirect" title="Defibrillator">defibrillator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Moderators were required to sign <a href="/wiki/Non-disclosure_agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-disclosure agreements">non-disclosure agreements</a> with Cognizant to obtain the job, although three former workers broke the agreements to provide information to <i>The Verge</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In the Tampa office, workers reported <a href="/wiki/Bed_bugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Bed bugs">bed bugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unsanitary" class="mw-redirect" title="Unsanitary">unsanitary</a> work conditions, inadequate mental health resources, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workplace_violence" title="Workplace violence">workplace violence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">theft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> As a result of exposure to videos depicting graphic violence, <a href="/wiki/Animal_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal abuse">animal abuse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a>, some employees developed <a href="/wiki/Psychological_trauma" title="Psychological trauma">psychological trauma</a> and posttraumatic stress disorder.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Cognizant sanitized the office before <i>The Verge</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s visit, a practice the publication described as a "<a href="/wiki/Dog_and_pony_show" title="Dog and pony show">dog-and-pony-show</a> phenomenon".<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup> In response to negative coverage related to its content moderation contracts, a Facebook director indicated that Facebook is in the process of developing a "global resiliency team" that would assist its contractors.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodies_in_Seats_131-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodies_in_Seats-131">[131]</a></sup></p><p>On October 30, Cognizant announced that it would phase out a portion of its content moderation contracts in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cognizant&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
